  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ef6c01d4-e103-4fb1-a4d7-d7a59d47b210'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer14825971154437278094">Kricket Hollowell is normally not one to wish upon stars; she believes they’re rarely in her favor. Well versed at dodging caseworkers from Chicago’s foster care system, the past few years on her own have made Kricket an expert at the art of survival and blending in. With her 18th birthday fast approaching, she dreams of the day when she can stop running and find what her </span>
  <span id="freeText14825971154437278094" style="display:none">Kricket Hollowell is normally not one to wish upon stars; she believes they’re rarely in her favor. Well versed at dodging caseworkers from Chicago’s foster care system, the past few years on her own have made Kricket an expert at the art of survival and blending in. With her 18th birthday fast approaching, she dreams of the day when she can stop running and find what her heart needs most: a home. <br /><br />Trey Allairis hates Earth and doubts that anyone from his world can thrive here. What he’s learning of Kricket and her existence away from her true home only confirms his theory. But, when he and Kricket lie together under the stars of Ethar, counting them all may be easier than letting her go. <br /><br />Kyon Ensin’s secrets number the stars; he knows more about Kricket's gifts than anyone and plans to possess her because of them. He also knows she’s more valuable than any fire in the night sky. He’ll move the heavens and align them all in order to make her his own. <br /><br />When everything in their world can be broken, will Kricket rely upon love to save her under different stars?</span>
  <a data-text-id="14825971154437278094" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">There is mature sexual content that is pretty tame but still obvious in all three books. Later on the graphic nature of the fighting gets a little mor<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">There is mature sexual content that is pretty tame but still obvious in all three books. Later on the graphic nature of the fighting gets a little more intense but nothing that I would keep from a middle-schooler. If I had to give it an age due to the mature nature, I would say 16 is a safe age. The Protagonist in this book is 17-18 throughout the series. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/1385931-annam"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1296401884i/1385931._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/1385931-annam">AnnaM</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">No. Not even an advanced one. There are way too many adult themes. It's not the sexual tension that makes me say this. It's the hints of past abuse, a<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">No. Not even an advanced one. There are way too many adult themes. It's not the sexual tension that makes me say this. It's the hints of past abuse, and the current dubious consent. The heroine may act and look like an adult but she is underage on both planets and many decades younger than all of the men who fall in lust with her, two of whom almost straight out tell her they don't care if she wants to marry/produce kids with them, too bad, she will have to as soon as they can get ceremony done. Even the hero undresses her completely while she's unconscious. No way would I let an 11 yr old read this.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=mary-sue">mary-sue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=jericho-fucking-barrons">jericho-fucking-barrons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=boring-main-character">boring-main-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=alpha-male">alpha-male</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer801148444" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11001663308607339104"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Kricket,” he grins. “It’s such a powerful name,” he breathes.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388213513ra/7767601.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>If a Kricket cries alone in a forest, does Khanh give a fuck? No. No, she doesn't. Who is Kricket? What is Kricket? I'll tell you.<br/><br/><b>Take the loveliest, most statuesque and Amazonian-like model you can find, then multiply her beauty tenfold.</b> Add some killer cheekbones to that vision of loveliness. Give her a brilliant brain whose intelligence is visible because her frontal lobe is all alight when viewed with special X-ray gla</span>
  <span id="freeText11001663308607339104" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Kricket,” he grins. “It’s such a powerful name,” he breathes.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388213513ra/7767601.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If a Kricket cries alone in a forest, does Khanh give a fuck? No. No, she doesn't. Who is Kricket? What is Kricket? I'll tell you.<br><br><b>Take the loveliest, most statuesque and Amazonian-like model you can find, then multiply her beauty tenfold.</b> Add some killer cheekbones to that vision of loveliness. Give her a brilliant brain whose intelligence is visible because her frontal lobe is all alight when viewed with special X-ray glasses! Have her be so slender that she can't rappel because the rope used for climbing down mountainsides can't support her bird-light weight (that doesn't even fucking make sense!!!!!!). Make her an orphan. Give her a special destiny. Make her so bloody special without knowing it.<br><br>That, my dear friends, is a fucking Kricket.<br><br>But that's not all, our Kricket's story doesn't end there, no. Her destiny is intertwined with several douchebags romantic leads, insta-love, a love triangle, and fucking aliens straight out of <i>Earth Girls are Easy</i>. There, in a nutshell, you've got <i>Under Different Stars</i>.<br><br><u>Summary</u>: Kricket is *sigh* an orphan. A tough-luck Orphan Annie. She's 17 (soon to be 18). She is hiding under the radar from the Chicago Department of Social Services, because beautiful girls like her can't survive in the foster system without being shanked because other girls hate her beauty so much that they'll hurt her for it (she's got the scars to prove it!).<br><br>So Kricket is lying low. <b>A little hard to do when you're 5'10, with platinum blonde hair, and violet eyes, but *sigh* what can a poor girl do?</b> She's working as a janitor despite having test scores good enough for admittance at the University of Michigan, Ann Arbor, because she can't afford the tuition. She also works at a bar under the table, because naturally, bars are so eager to lose their fucking liquor license by employing an underaged child and paying her under the fucking table.<br><br>Kricket is special. She can tell when people lie. Her hair (platinum blonde) grows back immediately after it's been cut.<br><br>When most people don't cut their hair ever, they look like this: <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388213513i/7767602.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>While Kricket, with her un-cuttable hair, looks like this: <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388213513i/7767603.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Did Kricket forget to tell us that her hair is platinum blonde? It's platinum blonde.<br><br>She's got a spicy, spicy gay Latino friend and his equally smexy and sassy boyfriend! Life sucks, but she deals. Until douchebags start coming after her for no fucking reason. They try to kidnap her every fucking where she goes (apparently, there are two groups of them) led by two guys: let's call them Asshole and Motherfucking Asshole, respectively. Asshole and Motherfucking Asshole proceed to lead Kricket on a merry motherfucking chase around Chicago, yelling random ass shit "you-will-pay-for-your-crimes!" to Kricket, but naturally, Kricket doesn't have a fucking clue what they're talking about.<br><br>And her hair is platinum blonde.<br><br>Finally, Asshole #1 (fine, his name is Trey) manages to kidnaps her using chloroform (which is actually a sweet scent that doesn't smell like ammonia, get your facts straight). He tells her jack shit. He looks into her eyes lovingly.<br><br>And her hair is platinum blonde.<br><br>Trey nearly drowns her. He tells her that a "crike" is fifty years. He hugs her.<br><br>He makes her rappel down a cave (smart) when she's hardly climbed more than the rock-climbing walls at her gym. He calls her Kitten. He sniffs her hair.<br><br>He takes her to an alien planet! He tells her nothing. He gently caresses her cheeks.<br><br>They run from wild animals and man-eating tigers. He tells her the etiquette between males and females. He tells her how brilliant she is.<br><br>Kricket almost sniffs a killer flower. Trey tells her not to! <b>They salsa-dance in the forest!</b> (I'm not fucking kidding)<br><br>They arrive in the promised land! Oh, finally, some information!!!! Kricket is important because she's the daughter of her mom! Her mom's a priestess! WELL THAT JUST EXPLAINS EVERYTHING. Her mom's like Helen, the face that launched a thousand ships! The woman who started a war! They started a war over her because she's powerful! Because she can, uh...<blockquote>
  <i>“What knowledge? Could she predict the future?”<br>“I don’t know what her gifts were, Kricket. It was never common knowledge.”</i>
</blockquote>Are you fucking kidding me? <b>These dumb as fuck aliens started a war over a woman whose skills are...unknown?</b> It's like starting a war over Iraq because of some random Weapons of Mass Destructions, man. It's fucking dumb.<br><br>And then they get to the special Palace where there's a fucking love triangle over the bigger dickwad who also tried to kidnap her! PLOT?! WHAT PLOT!!!!!!!!!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388213513i/7767604._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh, and Kricket's hair? It's platinum blonde.<br><br><u>The Setting</u>: AHAHAHAHA. AHAHAHAHAH. YOU'RE KIDDING ME, RIGHT? These fucking aliens are the dumbest piece of shit in the world. The world building is fucking silly, man.<br><br>I could tell you that I had a bambuzzle for hugglypoo, and then I went to gympilo to mumple my snortificus, in order to frumplefly my tigglebuns. Does that make any fucking sense? I was laughing my ass off because the language, the language! <b>Pick some random fucking ass words, pretend they're alien words with different meanings, and you've got the language of the Etharians!</b><blockquote>
  <i>“I’m heading straight to Sequelle’s and eating an entire venish.”<br>“No one can eat an entire venish.”<br>“I’ll take that wager. No Etharian can eat an entire venish,” Jax replies. “I’ll lay thirty-two fardrooms on it."<br>“Where are you going to get the money for a wigg?” Wayra laughs.<br>“I’ll start by taking yours, chester,” Jax counters.<br>“How many circas of vista did you give her, Trey?” Jax asks, sounding concerned again.</i>
</blockquote>By the way: <b>when a world has LESS gravity, you run slower, not faster</b>. Get your facts straight.<br><br>As for the world building of the aliens themselves, standard issue. Nothing imaginative. Nothing extraordinary. The only thing that stands out is how ridiculous and silly the faux-alien language is, and how juvenile the "soldiers" who kidnap Kricket are. They know about the internet. They know how to drive cars. They're aghast at the idea of nail polish! They're stupefied by the idea of a fucking thong.<blockquote>
  <i>“Can someone please tell me what that little pink, lacy thing is that I keep catching a glimpse of when she bends down?” Wayra asks.</i>
</blockquote><u>The Sound of a Single Kricket Chirping</u>: Oh, my! Kricket is so special! She's gorgeous (but doesn't know it). She could be a model (if only she were legal). <blockquote>
  <i>“Five-ten is not that tall.”<br>“C’mon, you look like a Viking. Those modeling agents would freak for your hollow cheekbones and I bet they’ve never seen a natural blond walk through their lobby doors.”</i>
</blockquote>Oh, ONLY 5'10. I'm only 5'4. Fuck you, Kricket. She's got platinum hair, which she reminds us at every fucking chance she's got.<blockquote>
  <i> while pulling my hat from my head, causing my long, platinum-blond hair to cascade around my shoulders.</i>
</blockquote>Oh, and her eyes! HER EYES! They're so freakish! Freakishly lovely!<blockquote>
  <i>“My eyes are not freakish!”<br>Enrique makes a derisive sound. “I’ve never met anyone with violet eyes,” he replies, raising his eyebrows. “If I had eyes like yours, I’d be in New York making some serious cash.”</i>
</blockquote>She's so smart! Soooooooo smart!<blockquote>
  <i>“So that means she’s smart?”<br>Jax beams. “Yeah, she’s smart! She’s brilliant! There’s no telling what she can do.”</i>
</blockquote>She's wise beyond her years! These aliens just KNOW this, man!<blockquote>
  <i>“You don’t act your age. You ask questions that I’d expect from someone older than you.”</i>
</blockquote>She's BRAVE! Because she knows how to run away from a dangerous monster! As if it's not a natural instinct, like what science calls a <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fight-or-flight_response" rel="nofollow noopener">"fight or flight"</a> reaction or anything.<blockquote>
  <i>Kissing my hair near my temple he whispers against it, “You’re so brave.”</i>
</blockquote>Kricket is special! SOOOOO SPECIAL! <blockquote>
  <i>"It’s like you were a special case from the start.”</i>
</blockquote>All because of her special parents! <blockquote>
  <i>“You’re a very important member of our clan,”<br>“What am I, royalty?”<br>“No…you’re much higher than that.” he replies, his eyes assessing me.</i>
</blockquote>MORE THAN ROYALTY! GAAAAAASP!!!!!<br><br>She's so fucking perfect that after days trampling through the fucking forest primeval, she's none the worse for wear except for a slight fucking tan.<blockquote>
  <i>I examine my reflection in the mirror for the first time in days. I can’t believe that I look almost the same. Apart from a tan, I can’t even tell that I’ve just been pulled through the universe to another one where I’m the enemy to just about everyone.</i>
</blockquote><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388213513ra/7767605.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>The Romance</u>: Let's just overlook the whole love triangle thing. I mean it. The love triangle is the least of this book's troubles when it come to romance. Frankly, the romance comes out of fucking nowhere. Trey fucking kidnaps Kricket. She protests, she yells halfheartedly, she doesn't seem to fucking mind. He takes her to another world. She doesn't give a fuck except to protest halfheartedly about killing him. <b>All of a sudden, he's touching her, caressing her, sniffing her hair, telling her that he's lost his heart to her. AND WE'RE NOT EVEN 25% INTO THE BOOK YET.</b><blockquote>
  <i>“You trying to stop her heart, sir?” Jax asks in a concerned tone, coming to me and checking me for injuries.<br>“No, she’s stopping mine,” Trey replies softly, watching Jax examine me.</i>
</blockquote>I don't quite know what to make of Trey, because Trey doesn't know exactly what he wants to be. He's got no personality. He's not quite a nice guy. He's not quite an asshole (although he sure as fuck tries to be one). He is just completely unnotable, absolutely fucking forgettable in every single way. He seems to ascribe specialness to the already special snowflake that is Kricket. He seems to enjoy playing <b>babysitter</b> to her than being her lover and her equal.<br><br>Halfway through the book, Kricket and Trey are already familiar enough with each other to simulate having sex to fool people. It's meant to be steamy, I guess? I laughed.<br><br><b>It's a fucking Herbal Essence commercial with all the moans and groans, guys.</b><blockquote>
  <i>Then, I close my eyes, groaning louder than before as water cascades down my hair. “Ohhh, Trey…Trey!” I call out in a raspy tone, like I’ve heard Bridget do in the middle of the night when Eric sleeps over. Finding a dispenser of shampoo, I pour some in my hand, lathering it in my hair. Eliciting what I hope is a sensual sounding gasp, I let my voice strain as I murmur, “Ahhh…” Rinsing my hair, I try the other dispenser that smells like coconut.</i>
</blockquote><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388213513i/7767606.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That picture isn't accurate. Kricket's hair is platinum blonde.</span>

<div id="review_1328898149" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1328898149" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1328898149?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/25890704-under-different-stars">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">No one</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Steph by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/8422973-stephanie-ideally-inspired">Stephanie • Ideally Inspired</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=why-the-hype">why-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=disappointment">disappointment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2015-release">2015-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=where-s-my-chocolate">where-s-my-chocolate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2015-reads">2015-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=could-have-been-better">could-have-been-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=didn-t-care-for-it">didn-t-care-for-it</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1328898149" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1495577647414235556">Welp. Another case of pretty cover and terrible book has struck me again. <br/><br/>Kricket is a super special girl. She has special powers, special eye color, special hair color, special name and spelling of said name. She's really beautiful, but doesn't know it and every guy wants her body for himself... some as old as dirt! She's also The One at the center of a prophecy her super special mom prophesized long, long ago in a galaxy far, far away. <br/><br/>Are you rolling your eyes yet? <br/><br/>Never have I read a book wi</span>
  <span id="freeText1495577647414235556" style="display:none">Welp. Another case of pretty cover and terrible book has struck me again. <br><br>Kricket is a super special girl. She has special powers, special eye color, special hair color, special name and spelling of said name. She's really beautiful, but doesn't know it and every guy wants her body for himself... some as old as dirt! She's also The One at the center of a prophecy her super special mom prophesized long, long ago in a galaxy far, far away. <br><br>Are you rolling your eyes yet? <br><br>Never have I read a book with so many ridiculous tropes balled up into one novel. Not that there is anything inherently wrong with tropes because even I have a certain weakness for some. For example, I fall prey to the "girl and boy hate each other, but slowly fall in love through forced interaction" trope every time and I'm not ashamed to admit it. But <i>Under Different Stars</i> reads like a self-indulgent writing experiment with absolutely no purpose. <br><br>While on the run from the department of social services, Kricket is abducted by a group of men who share the same violet eye color as her. They end up taking her to a different world, and surprise, surprise, she's an alien with powerful abilities that are highly sought after. She's immediately thrust into a world where females are valued as much as a prized show dog and whose vernacular verges on both corny and juvenile. <br><br>Yet despite being born with a vagina and thus seen as lesser than her male counterparts, every male she runs into wants her. Whether for political gain, selfish wants or sexual conquest, Kricket is a highly sought after commodity, and much of the novel is a pissing contest between various man folk. One that seems interesting at first, but quickly losses its appeal with every new suitor. <br><br>Though most of the novel takes place over the course of a week, possibly two if I'm being generous, Kricket manages to fall in love with one of her original captors, Trey. I can usually pick out who the love interest is from the very beginning and <i>Under Different Stars</i> didn't even bother making this remotely difficult, nor did it make an attempt to keep the lovers apart. As I previously stated, this novel is very self-indulgent and doesn't particularly care to stay the course of what was originally laid out in the beginning for the reader. <br><br>At one point Kricket confesses her love to Trey only to be rebuffed and in her words "friend-zoned" due to his already established previous engagement to a childhood friend, something she was well aware of beforehand. Yet, imagine my surprise when while Kricket is yet again fawning over Trey, claiming her undying love, and he AGAIN telling her no, that he suddenly tells her that he's broken it off with his fiancé and wants to be with her. And then an argument over who loves who the most ensues, ending with her basically begging him to deflower her and he saying he wants to marry her instead. Because nothing else matters but their love, guys! <br><br>Oh, kitten.<br>Oh, honey.<br>*makes out*<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438627924ra/15736710.gif" alt=" photo vomits_zpswcxxfvta.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's the first time I've ever read a scene that does a complete 180 with no warning whatsoever. <br><br>To say this <i>Under Different Stars</i> has a bad case of wish fulfillment is a complete understatement since Kricket can, in fact, wish her way out of certain circumstances. Whatever Kricket wants, she has the power to get. Kricket doesn't want to marry someone? No worries, another male suitor will have him killed. Kricket wants Trey to be with her and ditch his childhood sweetheart? So it shall be done. I mean, the amount of wank that went into this novel is shocking. <br><br>Kricket isn't the heroine of the story despite her situation. No, instead she is the heroine of the story because the world is setup to be terrible so she can be the shining ray of light. With so many male characters that belittle her and constantly want to control both her powers and body, Kricket is the stanch feminist who desires to be in control of her own destiny. While all the men attempt to mansplain to her, they later find out that she's actually a genius whose "brain lights up like a christmas tree" on a scanner. They frequently tell her how she can't defend herself and yet Kricket has the most powerful powers out of everyone. Everyone in the book is deliberately horrible, so she can look flossy as fuck.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438627924ra/15736711.gif" alt=" photo swim in vomit_zpsmxla3dxq.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>To make matters worse, the ratio of male to female characters is nauseating. Only three, including Kricket, have lines in the book and I'm pretty sure I can count on one hand how many times they chatted with each other one page. Two other female characters are mentioned, one being Kricket's dead mother and the other Trey's fiancé. Everyone else is virtually male or just not mentioned. Ugh.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Also, why is her name Kricket?! Why is she the only one with the super odd name? Why does she spell it with a K?? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>A part of me is confused, surprised and disgusted with myself for continuing to listen to the audiobook even when I knew there was no way possible for it to redeem itself with me, but I'm such a stubborn reader with a pinch of masochism. Maybe under different stars I could have liked this book, but it's made up of too many of the things I dislike to have ever had a chance. Such a shame because I really do love those covers. <br><br>More reviews and other fantastical things at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery</a>.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="1495577647414235556" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1170722397" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1170722397" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1170722397?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=aliens">aliens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=superpowers">superpowers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1170722397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1479123545697120084"><b>DNF'd at 22%</b><br/><br/>Call me crazy, but I had this perfect resolution to help me stop reading eight books at the same time this year and that was to <u>DNF books no more</u>. Because, see, when reading multiple books, you can easily find yourself losing interest for the first you had started and losing interest most of the time, for me, equals MEH equals DNF.<br/><br/>Needless to say, I failed my most essential bookish goal for 2015. No, let me rephrase that: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19504931.Under_Different_Stars__Kricket___1_' title='Under Different Stars (Kricket, #1) by Amy A. Bartol' rel='nofollow noopener'>Under Different Stars</a> made me fail my most essential bookish g</span>
  <span id="freeText1479123545697120084" style="display:none"><b>DNF'd at 22%</b><br /><br />Call me crazy, but I had this perfect resolution to help me stop reading eight books at the same time this year and that was to <u>DNF books no more</u>. Because, see, when reading multiple books, you can easily find yourself losing interest for the first you had started and losing interest most of the time, for me, equals MEH equals DNF.<br /><br />Needless to say, I failed my most essential bookish goal for 2015. No, let me rephrase that: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19504931.Under_Different_Stars__Kricket___1_" title="Under Different Stars (Kricket, #1) by Amy A. Bartol" rel="nofollow noopener">Under Different Stars</a> made me fail my most essential bookish goal for this year. Dramatic much? Well, it is the truth after all…<br /><br /><b>Kricket it oh so special.</b> No lies being told, because she 1) is Etharian (super important family), 2) has the detector of lies incorporated in her mind (<u>just like Emma from Once Upon a Time</u>) and 3) has freaking hair that grows instantaneously back after you cut it! Oh and HER HAIR, I didn’t do it justice. Let’s not forget how platinum, gorgeous and unearthly it is on top of having this regeneration ability. <br /><br />But what I didn’t tell you is that Kricket is one of the most annoying characters I have read in years. I’m usually one to avoid know-it-all, excessively curious and claiming innocence heroines because they just make me want to shut them off with a book thrown at their face. It’s not by portraying a character as such that you will make her/him sound more ‘intelligent’ or ‘interesting.’ Most likely, she/he will irritate the hell out of us, readers. At least, that’s how I feel about them, but I’m generalising, of course. We all love you, Hermione. (Although, Hermione is not one to repetitively claim innocence, of what I remember.) <br /><br />That being said, not liking a main character is a huge factor in DNFing a book. And so I did and freed myself from my misery consisting of putting up with that girl. But it wasn’t actually just that. I had hopes for a great romance, but Trey gave such contradictory signs. It’s like he was very understanding and cared for Kricket but simultaneously despised her. I mean, boy, decide.<br /><br />What also didn’t work for me was the writing style. It was too colloquial for the kind of story the author wrote and, because of that, most dialogs felt childish or unserious. <br /><br />It did start promisingly though. In a fast-paced way and already introducing us to some characters, which is something I like being done to catch the reader’s interest. <br /><br />But it all fell down, from that point onwards. Down down down. And so I wouldn’t recommend it, especially not if you’re looking for a fantastic science fiction YA read.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1479123545697120084" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1884858057" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10348951727194061760">When I read YA I usually don't look for the writing to be as complex as when something is supposed to be literature and I feel a lot more forgiving about cliches like the heroin being tall beautiful and blonde so that's probably why I liked this book more than others did. If a YA book has good pacing and a story line that keeps me engaged then usually I enjoy it. I liked the characters and yeah there were things that made you suspend your disbelief but I personally didn't find it hard to do so w</span>
  <span id="freeText10348951727194061760" style="display:none">When I read YA I usually don't look for the writing to be as complex as when something is supposed to be literature and I feel a lot more forgiving about cliches like the heroin being tall beautiful and blonde so that's probably why I liked this book more than others did. If a YA book has good pacing and a story line that keeps me engaged then usually I enjoy it. I liked the characters and yeah there were things that made you suspend your disbelief but I personally didn't find it hard to do so with this book, I don't think the author really wrote anything that made it hard for me to get into the story. I enjoyed it and I'm looking forward to reading the next one.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1103015113" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1103015113" />
    <a title="Pam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13865261-pam"><img alt="Pam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374039144p2/13865261.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1103015113?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pam" href="/user/show/13865261-pam">Pam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13865261-pam?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13865261-pam?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13865261-pam?shelf=5">5</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13865261-pam?shelf=bad-ass-chick">bad-ass-chick</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13865261-pam?shelf=suspense-chills-n-thrills">suspense-chills-n-thrills</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13865261-pam?shelf=sweeter-side">sweeter-side</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13865261-pam?shelf=fantastical">fantastical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13865261-pam?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13865261-pam?shelf=soldiers-n-uniforms">soldiers-n-uniforms</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1103015113" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10702349013484704588"><i>5 unforgettable stars</i><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Be careful what you wish for...”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427085810i/14179676.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/> <br/><b>
  <u>Kricket Hollowell</u>
</b> never fit in, running and making it on her own, she is counting down until her 18th birthday. On that day, she can finally be free, no longer on the run from social services. But one desperate night, one careless wish, she finds herself being hunted by two sets of men who seem to know more about her past that she herself. It turns out there was a reason all along as to why she never fit in, a gift from her m</span>
  <span id="freeText10702349013484704588" style="display:none"><i>5 unforgettable stars</i><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Be careful what you wish for...”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427085810i/14179676.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br><b>
  <u>Kricket Hollowell</u>
</b> never fit in, running and making it on her own, she is counting down until her 18th birthday. On that day, she can finally be free, no longer on the run from social services. But one desperate night, one careless wish, she finds herself being hunted by two sets of men who seem to know more about her past that she herself. It turns out there was a reason all along as to why she never fit in, a gift from her mother that has been passed down to her, a gift so valuable, making her wanted by all...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427085810i/14179677.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Two very dangerous men, with two different motives. Kyon, from the Alameeda Brotherhood, seems far to at ease when it comes to delivering a lie with a smile. Trey, a general from Skye, a Rafe citizen, seems to be the only one she can trust. At least he has been upfront with his intentions, even if they mean that she would be paying for crimes. Torn between her mother and father's people, Kricket the product of her parent's illicit love affair seems to be the trigger to the impending war between Rafe and Alameeda. While the other other houses need to decide who to allay themselves with, for it is inevitable and it seems that Kricket's gifts can be most useful. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Fortune favors the brave”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427085810i/14179678.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Trey and his most trusted men are belived to be the best of the best, so delivering a simple human female to the Reagent of Rafe should be easy now that they found her but they never anticipated for all that is Kricket. She has managed to surprise them and knock them off their feet; with her strength, charm and drive. And while Trey is driven by rules and orders, he can't help how protective and possessive he feels about Kricket. Even if she drives him mad. But under the stars when the walls are down, anything can happen and bloom. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You trying to stop her heart, sir?” Jax asks in a concerned tone, coming to me and checking me for injuries. <br><br>“No, she’s stopping mine,” Trey replies softly,</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427085810ra/14179679.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Finding herself in a dimension far from home, she knows she will survive this just like everything else in her life. But what will it costs her for the information she seeks, how far is she willing to go to get to know her parents... <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I’m stone. Nothing touches me—nothing</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427086108i/14179692._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But with men vying for her attention, with Kyon demanding her hand, the Regent playing with her as if she is a toy, and Trey the man that fills her heart and can easily break it...<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"...your voice will give comfort when the night becomes its blackest,” he replies. “And I’ll protect that voice with my body, my mind, and my spirit . . . because without it, I’m alone in the dark.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427085810ra/14179680.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Under Different Stars</b> is a fantastic ya-fantasy read, I was pulled in immediately, invited to live through each moment with Kricket. Her strength is also her weakness and that is what makes her come to life. Trey is a duty bound man, but has the inner struggle between what he is supposed to do and what his heart is telling him. I love the butterfly in my tummy feels, experiencing their need and longing; the battle between heart and mind. At times I forget that Kricket is only eighteen, she was forced to grow up early in life which made her the woman she is today. At first I was scared that there would be a love-triangle between Trey, Kricket and Kyon, but Kyon proved to be an ass from the moment he opened his mouth. <br><br>This story has the fantastical element of a science fiction novel, the beginning and growth of a true love, loyalty, friendship and political games. It is told from Kricket's POV, and I wish at times I could get into Trey's head, only to see what he was thinking. I absolutely loved it and cannot wait to read what happens next for Kricket. Recommended for those who see the beauty in the stars and wonder of a world so different from here...<br><br><i>ARC kindly provided by 47North, via NetGalley, in exchange for an honest review .</i><br> <br>***Quotes above are taken from the ARC version of the book and may differ upon publication.<br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="10702349013484704588" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer775144579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11607213886740165427"> <b>4,5 SCI-FI STARS<br/><br/> "You cannot thrive under the wrong stars, Kricket." </b><br/><br/>OMG this book was so captivating! I couldn't put it down, I was hooked from the first chapter! I am so in love with all the characters, this book has it all. Lots of action, romance, humor,and dystopian! Under Different Stars takes place on both Earth and an alternate planet called Ethar which lends to the sci-fi feeling. I love the world Amy creates, it's so interesting. Her descriptions of the people and places, especially o</span>
  <span id="freeText11607213886740165427" style="display:none"> <b>4,5 SCI-FI STARS<br><br> "You cannot thrive under the wrong stars, Kricket." </b><br><br>OMG this book was so captivating! I couldn't put it down, I was hooked from the first chapter! I am so in love with all the characters, this book has it all. Lots of action, romance, humor,and dystopian! Under Different Stars takes place on both Earth and an alternate planet called Ethar which lends to the sci-fi feeling. I love the world Amy creates, it's so interesting. Her descriptions of the people and places, especially on Ethar, help you picture this world. I really felt like I was there!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1389959978ra/8113192.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Kricket is a a 17-year-old girl who doesn't have any family but she has friends, however she knows that she is different from the others. She has violet eyes and she can tell when someone lies or tells the truth. One night while she's on the train on her way home from work she meets three very interesting and handsome men, but she knows that something is off about them, she manages to get away from them only to be attacked by three other guys. These men claim that they have been searching for her, and have a mission which involves returning her to the world she belongs to. <br><br>After a catch they manage to take her with them on an epic journey through caves, portals and jungles. The leader of the team is Trey Allairis. He is a military soldier who follows orders. His one and only objective, is to secure his target, and return her safely to her people. Trey soon learns that aside from dangerous creatures and threats from rival beings, there are bigger things he needs to watch out for. He also discovers that he may be getting more than he bargained for when it comes to Kricket Holloway, as he finds that she may just mean more to him than a “mission”... <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390165309i/8155700.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I liked Kricket so much! She was such a great female lead! She was so strong, she was a total badass! I think I have a big crush with her :))) Also she is tough and courageous! She isn't afraid to face her fears. She was honest, fun and absolutely lovable. <br>And Trey...I loved, loved, loved Trey. My attraction for him happened immediately!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390165309i/8155701.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Everything surrounding Trey and Kricket developed naturally and beautifully!<br>This is an amazing read! It was fast-paced, entertaining, with enough sexual tension!!<br>I cannot wait until the next book comes out! <br></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer786374856" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14654327798725824054">This was an okay YA sci-fi story, but it had quite a big slow patch, and a lot of info-dumping at the start.<br/><br/>Kricket was quite feisty and she certainly knew how to get herself into trouble. It seemed like trouble followed her around constantly, and she also had a real love of arguing, which to be honest irritated me a bit.<br/><br/>The storyline in this was okay, and there was some action, I had problems though. There was a massive chunk of the book which was really slowly paced, full of info-dumps, and al</span>
  <span id="freeText14654327798725824054" style="display:none">This was an okay YA sci-fi story, but it had quite a big slow patch, and a lot of info-dumping at the start.<br /><br />Kricket was quite feisty and she certainly knew how to get herself into trouble. It seemed like trouble followed her around constantly, and she also had a real love of arguing, which to be honest irritated me a bit.<br /><br />The storyline in this was okay, and there was some action, I had problems though. There was a massive chunk of the book which was really slowly paced, full of info-dumps, and also full of weird, poorly explained ‘alien’ words, and boy did that get old quick. Thankfully the book moved on a bit in the second half, and wasn’t quite so bad. Kricket seemed to have a lot of choices taken away from her in the second half of this book, and I did feel sorry for her a bit. <br /><br />There was some romance in this, although early on in the book I didn’t really get what this pair saw in each other as all they did was argue. Things did seem to develop in the second half of the book, and the romance improved a bit.<br /><br />The ending to this had a bit of action, which was good, but this book was still let down by all those info-dumps though.<br />6.5 out of 10<br /></span>

<div id="review_992768214" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/992768214" />
    <a title="Candace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16384209-candace"><img alt="Candace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459720769p2/16384209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/992768214?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/16384209-candace">Candace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/25890704-under-different-stars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=listened-to-audio-version">listened-to-audio-version</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=kidnapped">kidnapped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=dangerous-hero-themed-books-read">dangerous-hero-themed-books-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=forbidden-romance">forbidden-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=sweet-heart-warming-stories">sweet-heart-warming-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=shocking-twists">shocking-twists</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer992768214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18334063066576615127">Even though it isn't my usual genre, I've found myself reading a fair amount of paranormal YA books recently. Maybe I needed to change it up a bit to get out of a rut, or maybe it's just coincidental. Either way, there is something that has drawn me to this genre as of late and I'm working my way through many books that have been waiting for me on my TBR list for quite some time.<br/><br/>'Under Different Stars' is by far, one of the best books that I've run across in this genre. The heroine, Kricket, is </span>
  <span id="freeText18334063066576615127" style="display:none">Even though it isn't my usual genre, I've found myself reading a fair amount of paranormal YA books recently. Maybe I needed to change it up a bit to get out of a rut, or maybe it's just coincidental. Either way, there is something that has drawn me to this genre as of late and I'm working my way through many books that have been waiting for me on my TBR list for quite some time.<br /><br />'Under Different Stars' is by far, one of the best books that I've run across in this genre. The heroine, Kricket, is endearing right from the start. She's strong and has faced a great deal of adversity in her young life, being tossed around the foster care system after the death of her parents when she was a young child. She's the type of heroine that earns your admiration. She's definitely not a shrinking violet.<br /><br />When Kricket is abducted, and returned to her otherworldly he me planet, she fights it every step of the way. She has no recollection of this alien planet, Ethar, and has no intention of giving in without a fight. <br /><br />Soon, it becomes clear that there is more than one faction that wants to possess her. Whether they want to protect Kricket or exploit her abilities is unclear. Everyone in this strange new world seems to want a piece of her. Some for their own lustful desires, and some for much more malicious reasons. A war is brewing, and Kricket will have to choose a side soon.<br /><br />Despite the numerous men that Kricket has captivated, she remains transfixed by Trey, the man who led the mission to capture her and bring her back to this strange world. What began as abutted rivalry has grown into something more. First her kidnapper and jailor, Trey quickly imprinted himself on her heart and soul. <br /><br />Promised to another, Trey makes every effort to keep his feelings for Kricket a secret. Being with her would have political ramifications that neither of them could fully comprehend. So, he tries to be content as Kricket's bodyguard, looking over her and ensuring her safety.<br /><br />However, Kricket's ability to distinguish truth from lies, thwarts Trey's plan to keep his feelings hidden from her. He can't get away with lying to her and she soon exposes his lie. As the two make plans to secure a future together, the unthinkable happens. Their plans are circumvented by more powerful individuals, who would have Kricket for their own.<br /><br />Although this was an innocent story, intended for a younger audience, I enjoyed every minute of this story. It was action-packed and emotional. The characters were inspiring and easy to relate to. Innocent or not, I will definitely be continuing this story. I hope that Kricket and Trey can get their happily ever after, even if the whole world seems to be working against them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18334063066576615127" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5478965-aimee-aimee-always"><img alt="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562987681p2/5478965.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/781701252?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" href="/user/show/5478965-aimee-aimee-always">Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=covergasm">covergasm</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=arc">arc</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer781701252" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2851412643888868637"><a href='http://thesocialpotato.maryfaye.net/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421919725i/13429321._SX540_.png' alt=' photo UnderDifferentStarsbyAmyABartol_zpsa5c1039a.png' width='400px' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><p>
  <em>[DNF at 62%.]</em>
</p><br/><em>Under Different Stars</em> could have been a unique, engaging and intriguing read--<strong>unfortunately, the book fell flat for me</strong>. I've wanted to DNF this one lots of times before I actually did, probably because of the characters and the writing, mainly.<br/><br/>See, <strong>I've always had a strong dislike for books with formula characters</strong>. Kricket was your typical heroine--she was the beautiful (yes, she does look quite exotic with her purple eyes and blonde hair--*cringe*) girl who is apparently <em>sp</em></span>
  <span id="freeText2851412643888868637" style="display:none"><a href="http://thesocialpotato.maryfaye.net/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421919725i/13429321._SX540_.png" alt=" photo UnderDifferentStarsbyAmyABartol_zpsa5c1039a.png" width="400px" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><p>
  <em>[DNF at 62%.]</em>
</p><br><em>Under Different Stars</em> could have been a unique, engaging and intriguing read--<strong>unfortunately, the book fell flat for me</strong>. I've wanted to DNF this one lots of times before I actually did, probably because of the characters and the writing, mainly.<br><br>See, <strong>I've always had a strong dislike for books with formula characters</strong>. Kricket was your typical heroine--she was the beautiful (yes, she does look quite exotic with her purple eyes and blonde hair--*cringe*) girl who is apparently <em>special</em>. God,<strong> it's been a while since I've read a book that took <em>perfect</em> to an extreme, </strong>and I definitely did not appreciate it.<br><br><strong>Trey (you got it right--the love interest) was kind of a douche</strong>. I don't even use the word <em>douche</em> at all in real life (I hate how it sounds), but this guy is a special case. The dude fucking kidnapped Kricket! I get that he needed to, but come <em>on</em>. His two companions (who were really annoying flirts, by the way) at least, were humane about it. They joked with her and respected her needs. Trey? Not so much. Of course, that is until he <em>fell for her</em>.<br><br>Speaking of falling for her (ick), the romance was really disturbing and bland. <strong>I couldn't feel the "connection" between Kricket and Trey at all</strong>, probably because they went from cold to hot in just a matter of days, and without reason. Look at it this way: Trey kidnaps Kricket and of course, they fight about it. But then, out of nowhere, they're suddenly all touchy-feely with each other. Yeah, no thanks.<strong> And yes, there is sort of a love triangle</strong>, although I didn't get far enough to see how it progressed.<br><br>Another thing that bothered me was the annoying language and made-up words. I get it--they're on a different planet and will have different terms for things. But come on, <strong>why the hell would you want  to call somebody a "knob-knocker"?</strong> It sounds really trashy and immature.<br><br>I didn't even get far enough in the book to find out <em>if there even was a story</em>. But I have heard that the second half is just as bad as the first...</span>
  <a data-text-id="2851412643888868637" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_769288667" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/769288667" />
    <a title="Vilma Iris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15777655-vilma-iris"><img alt="Vilma Iris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501855386p2/15777655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/769288667?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vilma Iris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vilma Iris" href="/user/show/15777655-vilma-iris">Vilma Iris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer769288667" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1912024595452450357"><b>My newest all-consuming obsession and one of my absolute favorite books of the year! </b><br/>Utterly addicting, instantly absorbing and vividly depicted with intriguing and unforgettable characters. The story line is unique, suspenseful and brimming with the kind of scorching desire and idyllic romance that lingers with you long after the book ends.<br/><br/>**************************<br/><br/>Amy Bartol is dangerous. She writes nothing less than the kinds of books that make you want to keep your eyes open with toothpicks </span>
  <span id="freeText1912024595452450357" style="display:none"><b>My newest all-consuming obsession and one of my absolute favorite books of the year! </b><br>Utterly addicting, instantly absorbing and vividly depicted with intriguing and unforgettable characters. The story line is unique, suspenseful and brimming with the kind of scorching desire and idyllic romance that lingers with you long after the book ends.<br><br>**************************<br><br>Amy Bartol is dangerous. She writes nothing less than the kinds of books that make you want to keep your eyes open with toothpicks and ignore the world until you read the very last page. Forget the shower. Forget your children. Eating… optional. Sleeping… forget about it. All I can focus on is finishing her books. And this one… it was amazing! As addictive as the Premonition series. The angst, the romance, the desire as thick and enthralling as that of Evie and Reed. How the heck will I suffer through the months to get her next book? Her words literally get under my skin, her storytelling is so expressively captivating that I feel like a crazy, obsessive mad woman when I read her stories. You will LOVE Under Different Stars. LOVE. She manages to build this unique world full of crazy lingo and vivid details that had me hanging on to her every word. THEN, she throws two people together and builds this intensifying, oh-so-right desire between them that had me desperately needing them to be together more than I need my next breath. How does this woman do it?! I was enraptured by this story. I didn’t want it to end. It had action, humor, romance, desire and that intangible magic that Amy sprinkles throughout to enliven it, making us thoroughly addicted and begging for more.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“You cannot thrive under the wrong stars, Kricket… the stars here are in opposition to you… can’t you feel it?… Let us take you home.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Kricket has had a tough childhood, particularly in the foster care system. Now, she’s trying to just hold on to the last few months before she turns 18 when she’ll be finally free to live her own life and stop running. At 5′ 10″ with platinum blonde hair and violet eyes, Kricket is striking and has to work extra hard to stay under the radar by working jobs that pay in cash. When suddenly an unfamiliar trio of incredibly tall, incredibly good-looking men with the same violet eyes as hers find her and claim to be there to take her back “home,” Kricket is simultaneously shocked and on alert. She runs. Unfortunately, shortly after, she finds herself face-to-face with another ominous trio claiming the very same thing. It quickly becomes evident that there’s no place to run, no place she can hide. The first trio have found her again and she’s brusquely taken. As she grapples heart and mind to assess her situation and prepare once again for the worst, she can’t help but feel like her life is in constant turmoil… another situation of which she needs to figure out how to gain control.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“I’m used to holding on to nothing as tight as I can.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>The three men — Trey, Wayra and Jax — are on a mission to find her and bring her home… to Ethar. They claim it’s Kricket’s rightful homeland and it’s time for her to return and pay her penance. Incredulous and baffled, she can’t begin to make sense of what they’re talking about and even how they talk. Their lingo is different and Earth is not native to where they are from. The more time she spends with them as they trek back to Ethar, the more she’s drawn to their humor and even their kindness. The person who seems to be the leader of the group, Trey, is especially protective, although intriguing and somewhat firm, she can tell he’s telling her the truth.<br><br>You see, Kricket has this innate ability to irrevocably know when someone is lying. A gift she can’t explain. Kricket is truly a wonderful, kick-ass, witty heroine. She’s incredibly intelligent, inquisitive, funny, tenacious and with a strong sense of survival. The boys from Ethar seem to be equally intrigued with her. I loved seeing the dynamic between them evolve from distrust to trust to caring… especially with Trey. Circumstances continue to push them together as a mutual trust, respect and caring for each other slowly begins to blossom.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“I open my eyes and gaze at Trey next to me. He has his arms crossed behind his head as he stares up at the brilliant stars in the clear, night sky. He seems almost ethereal, bathed as he is in the bluish glow of the light stick. The warmth I felt earlier comes back, slipping through me and filling me with another kind of glow that calms my fear. Feeling his radiating body heat, my breathing slows. He’s too perfect looking to be real. This has to be a dream after all.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Amy Bartol is the queen of the slow burn… the intensifying angst… the building of emotion. The desire and longing that grows between them on this unexpected journey is unsettling as Kricket finds herself begin to feel more than she’s ever allowed herself to feel. As is also typical with this author, danger is always a breath away and each action scene pushes the characters even closer together. When they realize they are being pursued, the urgency is heightened and getting to Rafe becomes critical.<br><br>We learn that Ethar is comprised of five houses… Rafe, Alameeda, Comantre, Peney and Wurthem. We also learn that Kricket is a special type of anomaly that makes her valuable, especially to Kyon, one of the members of the other trio that sought her in Chicago. There are so many questions still to answer, however, and despite Trey’s candor, there’s so much left to uncover. One thing that is clear at this point is that her feelings for Trey have escalated so much more. His presence is comfort, his arms are protection and his touch ignites an irrepressible yearning.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Responding intellectually to his touch, desire is rising fiercely within me and with it, a ripple of fear is running through me as well because I’ve never felt passion like this before. It’s burning me, consuming me, and leaving almost no room for thought.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Trey is such an alluring character. He’s an enigma. He can be mercurial at times, embracing the emotions that continue to build between him and Kricket one moment and then pushing her away the next. Is she just a mission? Is she more? Does he really care?<br><br>When the time finally nears for her to be handed over at Rafe, a crushing feeling consumes as the uncertain becomes a certainty. And when she’s taken from her friends… from Trey, everything begins to crumble and she realizes she’s a pawn who is highly sought after with gifts that only certain people can expound on. As truths are also revealed about Trey, her heart begins to break in disillusionment.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“A familiar pain squeezes my heart. I know better than to let myself become attached to anyone, like I’ve allowed myself to become to Trey, but it happened too fast to avoid it.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>What ensues is a heart-stopping, heart-aching series of events that had me furiously flipping pages to see what would happen next. One thing is for sure though, by this point I am IN LOVE with Trey Allairis. The fierceness he exhibits, the protectiveness he shows, the gentleness of his actions and perhaps most significantly, his new proclivity for defying all the rules shows how much he loves Kricket. I was totally swooning over this man.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“I’d break every rule for you.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>AND… when Kricket challenges him once again, questioning his feelings for her, he says something like this…<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“No, I believe I said it was impossible for you to love me. Almost as impossible as hiding the fact that I love you.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Sigh.<br><br>I was sad to read the last page. I just didn’t want this book to end. I don’t have sufficient eloquent, descriptive words to convey how good this book is. SO MUCH HAPPENS. There are still so many secrets left to uncover as it ends on a precipice… on a promise of something more. Threats continue to loom and I am dying to have the next book in my hands. At this point, Amy Bartol has me groveling, begging, needing both Iniquity (from the Premonition Series) and Kricket’s second novel. I’m not sure what I’ll do with myself while I anxiously await her next utterly addictive story. There’s romance, suspense, action and drama and I can’t imagine anyone not loving this book. It’s a story about finding your truth, controlling your destiny and fiercely fighting for the kind of love that’s written in the stars.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“We have to make the stars align for us now — find a way for us not to get burned for being together.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1381417425i/4836951._SX540_.png" width="361.33" height="228.67" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>For more reviews, connect with me: <br><a href="www.vilmasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Vilma's Book Blog</a> | <a href="www.facebook.com/chitchatbookblog" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="www.twitter.com/vilmairis" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a></b></span>
