<div id="review_801728125" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/801728125" />
    <a title="Shelly Crane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5614044-shelly-crane"><img alt="Shelly Crane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1359264053p2/5614044.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/801728125?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelly Crane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelly Crane" href="/user/show/5614044-shelly-crane">Shelly Crane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5614044-shelly-crane?shelf=best-books">best-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer801728125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2681638948131686556">If you know me, you know how I adore my Amy Bartol. A lot. It could be classified as an obsession. She's all-around amazing.<br/><br/>But we're not going to talk about Bartol, we're going to talk about her amazing book. And this review is completely unbiased! I don't have a lot of reading time so I'm very stingy and picky with the books I read. So when I was given (begged for) this ARC of UDS, Amy said no pressure. Now, the book's been out for weeks and I'm finally able to get to it and I'm KICKING myself</span>
  <span id="freeText2681638948131686556" style="display:none">If you know me, you know how I adore my Amy Bartol. A lot. It could be classified as an obsession. She's all-around amazing.<br /><br />But we're not going to talk about Bartol, we're going to talk about her amazing book. And this review is completely unbiased! I don't have a lot of reading time so I'm very stingy and picky with the books I read. So when I was given (begged for) this ARC of UDS, Amy said no pressure. Now, the book's been out for weeks and I'm finally able to get to it and I'm KICKING myself for not making myself lose a night of sleep sooner! (4am)<br /><br />Holy Hot Alien Trey, Batman! He was fighting it so hard in the beginning, poor guy. Trying to do the right thing. And then kept on trying to do the right thing, but Kricket kept right on inching her way into his world and his heart until she was there to stay. He was an aggressive, strong, alpha, tattooed, military leader, good guy, rake you with his eyes kind of guy that was blind-sided by this girl who turned out to be nothing like they imagined she would when they went to find her. He gets so frustrated with her, but it's because he wants what he cant have, he wants to protect her, he knows that things are about to go bad real fast when they get 'home', and he'd being pulled in several directions. I felt for him. Even when he was mad at her and being an idiot, I could still understand the struggle. But he would always come back around and make you forget it in not time. He was so alpha and I love that. Her protection was the most important thing above all else and when she was in danger all his walls fell down, and you'd see his true feelings, even though sometimes Kricket couldn't even see them. And his little cute jealous ticks with their friends and the other 'suitors'. Adorable. When he decides something, look out, cause that boy is determined. He is my favorite book boy of the year.<br /><br />The app on my phone almost short circuited because of the heat between these two. I'll name a few instances. The pool, when Trey "saves her". I love when Jax tries to take her and Trey is not having any of it. Two, shower scene that was so, so hot but nothing actually happened at all. It broke my and Kricket's heart at the same time. Like...whoa. Instance number three, the first time he calls her Kitten...and anytime following that. Four, the fountain. Five, when he tells her what he did the night after the fountain in regards to a certain female and the whole 'missed birthday' conversation. Six, "Undergarments? Is that what you call those polar little monsters?" You get the gist of that one. So hot and swoony and adorable.<br /><br />"You can trust me with your heart."<br /><br />And Kricket, oh Kricket. Poor girl. Been to hell and back again and no one even bothered to buy her a t-shirt for her troubles. I loved her, too. She was spunky without being stupid. She never did these outrageous'y idiotic things to get into trouble where she had to be rescued or anything. She didn't let them walk all over her, but she cried and had moments where it was all too much. She was 'human' and though this was a fantasy book, it was real. I wanted to take her for coffee and get some names of people to kick butts of. She was awesome. She tried so hard to be brave and strong, to do what was the right thing, not just whatever her little heart desired. She wasn't selfish. She understood that there was a big picture to this whole thing. She understood sacrifice.<br /><br />And I LOVED the supporting cast. I mean LOVED them. That hardly ever happens for me. Like ever. Jax and Wayra were my absolute favorite. We didn't see Trey's brother Victus very much, but I know he'll be back. And I'm sure they'll be drama there, because it was hinted at. Maybe the family will want him to commit to Kricket and he may even have a crush on her himself, who knows. Trey's first intended, Charisma, we never saw (hallelujah!) but I'm pretty sure that won't last. She'll probably come back in book 2 as well, maybe even with a vengeance, but I'm happy with how things went. I was so, so, so happy that Trey didn't pull some parading-Charisma-around-in-front-of-Kricket stunt to hurt her and try to get her to move on. I waited for it and just knew it was coming but was so happy that Amy didn't follow the predictable route. I can't stand when couples try to use that stuff on each other when they love each other, even if they 'think' it's for a good reason. I hate it. So, bravo, Amy for not falling prey to typical YA cliches.<br /><br />This book was about a dystopian society. It was fascinating to read all about the things, words, food, animals, tons of things that Amy created for it. If you love to sink into a completely new world, then this is for you. Lots of romance and laughs. I literally could not put it down. You need to read this.<br /><br />I'm in love with paranormal\dystopian again!<br /><br />6 out of 5 stars from me!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2681638948131686556" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1147901768" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1147901768" />
    <a title="Rhea Dsouza" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19034087-rhea-dsouza"><img alt="Rhea Dsouza" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526584546p2/19034087.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1147901768?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rhea Dsouza" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rhea Dsouza" href="/user/show/19034087-rhea-dsouza">Rhea Dsouza</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19034087-rhea-dsouza?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19034087-rhea-dsouza?shelf=file-13">file-13</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19034087-rhea-dsouza?shelf=hbt-reviews">hbt-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1147901768" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10748178339040916442"><u>
  <b>How To Check If You’re An Alien Living on the Wrong Planet:</b>
</u><br/><br/>•	Your hair grows back immediately after it’s been cut. As in, a second later. And yet, after 17 years of living through this phenomenon, you have shoulder length hair. <br/><br/>•	You have violet eyes. <br/><br/>•	Your frontal lobe has X-ray vision.<br/><br/>•	You are so thin, so lightweight, so delicate that wall climbing harnesses can’t support you.<br/><br/>•	When a world has less gravity, you run faster instead of slower.<br/><br/>•	You get bossed around by three men and fall i</span>
  <span id="freeText10748178339040916442" style="display:none"><u>
  <b>How To Check If You’re An Alien Living on the Wrong Planet:</b>
</u><br><br>•	Your hair grows back immediately after it’s been cut. As in, a second later. And yet, after 17 years of living through this phenomenon, you have shoulder length hair. <br><br>•	You have violet eyes. <br><br>•	Your frontal lobe has X-ray vision.<br><br>•	You are so thin, so lightweight, so delicate that wall climbing harnesses can’t support you.<br><br>•	When a world has less gravity, you run faster instead of slower.<br><br>•	You get bossed around by three men and fall in love with their leader who, as it turns out, was the biggest jerk of them all.<br><br>•	Said leader also enjoys being your guardian/protector/sugar daddy more than being your lover. <br><br>•	Your other alien buddies know about (and browse) FACEBOOK but each want a piece of your undies.<br><br><br><b>
  <u>She’s my Cherry Pie, cool drink of water such a sweet surprise.</u>
</b><br><br>If you’ve gotten at least 50% of the above checklist right, then obviously your name is Kricket. You’re an orphan who is originally from the planet Ethar and your parents sent you to Earth for safekeeping…? I don’t even know. You’re a special one, did you know that? Like a four leaved clover. You have platinum hair. You have violet eyes. You’re also underage and working at a bar but that’s okay. You’re the female lead of the story after all. No harm can befall you, my dear.<br><br><br><u>
  <b>So I mixed up the batter and she licked the beater.</b>
</u><br><br>Turn away, ye lovers of romance. Because there isn’t any here. Under Different Stars is chock full of BS but there isn’t even a blip of romance. Sure there’s plenty of coercion, drowning, salsa in the forest, cheek caressing and fake sex. But romance? Nope.<br><br>Romance requires foundation. It requires feeling of attraction, lust. It does not happen when you get kidnapped (and really don’t mind it, know that I think about it) and out of a sudden, your kidnapper is your sweetheart. And the love interest? Trey? Jesus. He’s got no personality, nothing that you can remember him by, and just seems to be a great big know-it-all.<br><br><br><u>
  <b>You ain’t gonna swing with my <s>daughter</s> no more.</b>
</u><br><br>Introduce love interest #2. Kyon Ensin. Actually, he’s a bit of a villain too. Except, he seemed to me to have more character than anyone else in this wretched excuse for a novel. And if the next book is going to bring in a love triangle (which I’m sure it will), then remember; You saw it at first at Rhea’s Neon Journal (or Rhea’s Goodreads or Rhea’s Amazon wherever you read this)!<br><br><br><b>
  <u>Dirty, Rotten, Filthy, Stinkin!</u>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1093127600?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" href="/user/show/4197769-jacqueline-s-reads">Jacqueline&#39;s Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jacqueline's Reads by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/16453761-tricia-santos">Tricia  Santos</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1093127600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5856050949327264246"><b>4 Kickin’ Kricket Stars</b><br/><br/>It’s been awhile since I’ve read an Amy Bartol book. I wanted something light, a little romantic and plenty of action. I believe I got that with Under Different Stars.<br/><br/>This is a young adult read and the thing I love about young adult reads is the world I’m taken to. I love learning new languages, cultures and I know it’s going to be at least a three book saga. BUT that’s just me.<br/><br/>So Kricket currently lives on earth. She’s human or so she thinks. She knows she is a little dif</span>
  <span id="freeText5856050949327264246" style="display:none"><b>4 Kickin’ Kricket Stars</b><br><br>It’s been awhile since I’ve read an Amy Bartol book. I wanted something light, a little romantic and plenty of action. I believe I got that with Under Different Stars.<br><br>This is a young adult read and the thing I love about young adult reads is the world I’m taken to. I love learning new languages, cultures and I know it’s going to be at least a three book saga. BUT that’s just me.<br><br>So Kricket currently lives on earth. She’s human or so she thinks. She knows she is a little different. When she cuts her hair, it automatically grows back. She rides the subway one day and runs into Trey. Trey is hired to bring Kricket back to home and home is not on earth.<br><br>A good portion of the book is Kricket traveling back home. It’s a big slow at some parts, but you get immerse into the other world fairly quickly. Also, there’s a lot to learn. I felt like I needed a cheat sheet. I didn’t understand why they couldn’t just pounds and hours, but other words. I know I said I like learning new languages, but there was a lot!<br><br>So Trey and his buddies are traveling with Kricket and she is feisty. She’s the type of Heroine I like to read in these sci-fi books, very strong and opinionated, but not annoying. Once they reach home, the pace quickens a bit and oh my goodness, the sexual tension between Kricket and Try is nice. Get your mind out of the gutter, it’s a YA, so there’s only so much sexual tension, but I did blush at some of the scenes.<br><br>It was really cute.<br><br>I kind of wanted Trey and Kricket’s relationship to be dragged out a bit, I know I said the book was a bit slow. I just can’t make up my mind.<br><br>Overall, If you want something a little new, a little different and you haven’t read a Bartol novel, start with this one.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19504931.Under_Different_Stars__Kricket___1_" title="Under Different Stars (Kricket, #1) by Amy A. Bartol" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1394758272s/19504931.jpg" alt="Under Different Stars (Kricket, #1) by Amy A. Bartol" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B00HCJX2PM/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=211189&amp;creative=373489&amp;creativeASIN=B00HCJX2PM&amp;link_code=as3&amp;tag=jacqsread-20&amp;linkId=WIZPG2JDHEKFB37B" rel="nofollow noopener">AMAZON</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5856050949327264246" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_988316135" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/988316135" />
    <a title="Lazaros" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22313662-lazaros"><img alt="Lazaros" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578697302p2/22313662.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/988316135?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lazaros" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lazaros" href="/user/show/22313662-lazaros">Lazaros</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781493780556" href="/book/show/20595764-under-different-stars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=aliens">aliens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer988316135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15446965482524160030">Good, but nothing special.<br/><br/>I know Amy A. Bartol. She's not an unknown author to me. I've read her Premonition series and I am pretty familiar with her prose. In this book, she tried to step out her waters, and tried to do something more original than today's young-adult books.<br/><br/>Kricket is a troubled girl, a run away from the system, a girl with no family. Her life is not interesting. That changes when two groups of people come looking for her and is captured by one of those groups and brought to an</span>
  <span id="freeText15446965482524160030" style="display:none">Good, but nothing special.<br /><br />I know Amy A. Bartol. She's not an unknown author to me. I've read her Premonition series and I am pretty familiar with her prose. In this book, she tried to step out her waters, and tried to do something more original than today's young-adult books.<br /><br />Kricket is a troubled girl, a run away from the system, a girl with no family. Her life is not interesting. That changes when two groups of people come looking for her and is captured by one of those groups and brought to an alien world.<br /><br />Yes, yes, I forgot to tell you about Kricket's gift, that she knows when someone's lying to her. Or the fact that the her hair when cut, it turns from blond to dark and then turns to dust. Then it grows back to the same length it was before. <br /><br />We learn about Kricket's lineage, about the planet called Ethar, about its system, and how big it is, the differences with earth. Now, it's time I tell you the reason why this was not as good as it could be. It's a simple one: the author clearly didn't put much effort in creating an alien world as one would expect it. The so called Ethar is nothing but an Earth with a slightly different vocabulary. <br /><br />This could have been a really good book if only Mrs. Bartol would have taken care of its content. I didn't like the instant-love thingy, and that seems to be her thing. While she writes good romances, instead of building it up slowly, she just goes and makes it instant and rush. <br /><br />The end has no cliffhanger whatsoever. For a first book in a series it was really poor, from all aspects, but I enjoyed it nonetheless. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15446965482524160030" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1413646543" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Saania Zee Jamal ϟ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10376232-saania-zee-jamal"><img alt="Saania Zee Jamal ϟ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495529362p2/10376232.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1413646543?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Saania Zee Jamal ϟ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Saania Zee Jamal ϟ" href="/user/show/10376232-saania-zee-jamal">Saania Zee Jamal ϟ</a>

          marked it as not-gonna-bother




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10376232-saania-zee-jamal?shelf=ya-fantasy-romance">ya-fantasy-romance</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1413646543" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4070011756538700951">Gorgeous cover? <b>Check.</b><br/>Young adult fantasy? <b>Check.</b><br/>High average rating? <b>Check.</b><br/><br/><i>BINGO.</i><br/><br/>...or not.<br/>Definitely not.<br/><br/>In fact, the book completely misses the target as far as originality goes and aims for recycled, overdone, badly written, clichéd tropes convoluted to draw you in before you realize it's nothing but a trick.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444537973i/16514259.jpg' width='400' height='224' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Honestly, I'm so mad because I thought I'd chanced upon a hidden gem with those shining 4.29 stars it holds - up until I read a few trusted reviews and excerpts that were enough to convi</span>
  <span id="freeText4070011756538700951" style="display:none">Gorgeous cover? <b>Check.</b><br>Young adult fantasy? <b>Check.</b><br>High average rating? <b>Check.</b><br><br><i>BINGO.</i><br><br>...or not.<br>Definitely not.<br><br>In fact, the book completely misses the target as far as originality goes and aims for recycled, overdone, badly written, clichéd tropes convoluted to draw you in before you realize it's nothing but a trick.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444537973i/16514259.jpg" width="400" height="224" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Honestly, I'm so mad because I thought I'd chanced upon a hidden gem with those shining 4.29 stars it holds - up until I read a few trusted reviews and excerpts that were enough to convince me of what it <i>actually</i> was.<br><br>Sigh. Authors, when will you learn?</span>

<div id="review_768978352" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/768978352" />
    <a title="Gabi Daniels" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12939467-gabi-daniels"><img alt="Gabi Daniels" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349179821p2/12939467.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/768978352?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabi Daniels" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabi Daniels" href="/user/show/12939467-gabi-daniels">Gabi Daniels</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12939467-gabi-daniels?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer768978352" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8017040469786770026">5 STARS IS NOT ENOUGH!!<br/><br/>Honestly, the world building and original ideas Amy came up with could easily put this book in either the sci-fi or fantasy genres. It was that well done. I’m all with my swoony romance… but I read just as much sci-fi and dark fantasy to say that I could put this novel up against any of the novels I’ve read.<br/><br/>Captivating from page #1, I want to know more, more, more! Why is she on the run? Where is her family? How is she surviving on her own?<br/><br/>This incredibly intense story unf</span>
  <span id="freeText8017040469786770026" style="display:none">5 STARS IS NOT ENOUGH!!<br /><br />Honestly, the world building and original ideas Amy came up with could easily put this book in either the sci-fi or fantasy genres. It was that well done. I’m all with my swoony romance… but I read just as much sci-fi and dark fantasy to say that I could put this novel up against any of the novels I’ve read.<br /><br />Captivating from page #1, I want to know more, more, more! Why is she on the run? Where is her family? How is she surviving on her own?<br /><br />This incredibly intense story unfolds at the PERFECT pace. From slowly discovering and accepting that she isn’t human, to figuring out who to trust, and plotting how the hell to get herself out of all this craziness.<br /><br />When Kricket first arrived on Ethar (I want to go ga-ga over how they traveled, but I don’t want to spoil one of the coolest scenes I’ve ever read!), we discovered this new planet with Kricket. Amy described it’s beauty in such a way that I could vividly picture it; Redwood-like trees as tall as skyscrapers, weird and terrifying creatures, the night sky.<br /><br />And, of course, it’s a totally advanced civilization. Their technology was incredible! Kricket couldn’t figure out half the gadgets. It was ALMOST as funny as Trey &amp; gang trying to figure out the American slang Kricket used.<br /><br />Yet, the society’s views on “class” and women is backwards. This is all unacceptable to Kricket. But, being the survivor she is, she bides her time, played nice, and formed alliances where she needed to.<br /><br /><br />I fell in love with Kricket immediately. Despite the fact that she’s been in the foster care system since she was five and brutally abused– she’s so strong, compassionate, fiercely loyal to the only two friends she has on Earth, and is the definition of a survivor! BOOYAH!<br /><br />She also has understandable and significant trust issues, and a deep-rooted fear of abondonment that comes out at times when she is desperately trying to be or remain independent.<br /><br />This is an exchange between Kricket and Trey:<br /><br />“It will take a very hard, very determined personality to survive what is ahead for you without help.”<br /><br />“Got it,” I growl through clenched teeth, anger flaring up in me at the sympathy in his voice.<br /><br />“You’re tough?”<br /><br />“I’m stone.”<br /><br />“Stone can be broken.”<br /><br />Tilting my head toward him, I meet his eyes. “Don’t worry about me. I’ll be fine. I’m used to holding on to nothing as tight as I can.”<br /><br />I was so emotional by this point, I had to set my Kindle down for a while after I read that. This poor girl. Pushing away the only 3 people she knows on the planet. Why? Because she refuses to accept help. Worse! Be pitied. It’s not even about having a wall of protection… she’s got no wall. It’s raw. All of it; Pain, abuse, multiple disappointments, being just another number is the system. And this is why I absolutely love Amy’s writing– Instead of giving up and wallowing in it all, Kricket keeps it fresh. A reminder. She uses her past to build HERSELF up and strive for a better future.<br /><br />That said, accepting help and depending on Trey is setting herself up for another blow. Plus, she can take care of herself.<br /><br />Up until this point they shared a few tender moments. But it was this part when Trey’s professional, all-business military badass front came down a little. Said a different way, he likes her. A lot. <br /><br />Full review and character profile of Trey at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://gabidaniels.com/2013/12/17/review-of-under-different-stars-by-amy-bartol-character-profile-huge-giveaway/">http://gabidaniels.com/2013/12/17/rev...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8017040469786770026" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1325835806002471594" style="display:none"> ★★★★<br />I will admit I was mad that I had to read this book for a challenge featuring aliens. It's on the shelf so<br />I went with this one and I found a gem.<br /><br />Krickett Hallowell was a17 yr old foster kid runaway trying to stay out of sight until she is 18 and out of the system. Krickett ends up leaving with Trey Allairis and his companions because he was honest with her. <br /><br />Krickett had a special gift to discern truth and now she was a pawn for two political factions claiming her as kin. I love young love especially of the forbidden kind. I also liked the world the author created outside of earth. It was intriguing, and I found myself engaged the whole time.<br /><br />I love Kate Rudd as a narrator so I am ready for book 2.</span>

  </i>
</blockquote><br />This story is told through the eyes of Kricket Holloway, a 17-year-old girl who has spent her life in and out of the “system” after becoming an orphan as a young child. Her whole life she’s realized that she had certain traits that set her apart from ‘normal’ people. Despite her special abilities, she’s managed to fly under the radar undetected, while growing up in and out of foster homes within Chicago. One day she has a run-in with some men who claim to have been searching for her, and have a mission which involves returning her to the world in which she belongs…unfortunately, Kricket is neither willing, nor compliant, and is in need of further “persuation” (AKA, abduction). After playing a game of Cat &amp; Mouse, Kricket finds herself punching a one-way ticket aboard the “Rafe-Express”, which leads to an epic journey through portals, jungles, and caves. Spelunking, anyone? Did I mention that this trip includes 3 hot, other-worldly male tour guides? Can’t leave that out!<br /><br />The leader of Operation: <i>“Retrieve Kricket”</i> is a hunky hunk of a man by the name of Trey Allairis. He is a high-ranking military soldier who follows orders, and asks no questions. His one and only objective, is to secure his target, and return her safely to her people. This means that she is come back alive, and in one piece. You’d think that would be easy, right? WRONG! Trey soon learns that aside from dangerous creatures and threats from rival beings, there are bigger things he needs to watch out for. He also discovers that he may be getting more than he bargained for when it comes to Kricket Holloway, as he finds that she may just mean more to him than a “mission”.<br /><br />Throughout the course of this book, we follow Kricket who begins to blossom as she grows into her own. The more she learns about this new world that she will now become a part of, she sees that she must become vigilant, as everything is not as it seems. She must show that she is a force to be reckoned with.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“You’re tough?” “I’m stone.” “Stone can be broken.” Tilting my head toward him, I meet his eyes. “Don’t worry about me. I’ll be fine. I’m used to holding on to nothing as tight as I can.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“I underestimated you, Kricket,” Kyon says softly. “You’re so much more than I could have imagined.” “What?” I ask, startled by his compliment. “Having to fight all your life hasn’t made you less…it has made you more.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />Kricket is not only coming into her own and developing her powers, she is also learning to cope with her feelings that have developed for her captor-turned-savior-turned-advisor: Trey. Talk about a SLOW. BURN. Good grief. Those too could steam up my kindle without even touching each other. Their chemistry is out of this world…<i>
  <b>LITERALLY</b>
</i>! See what I did there? Cause…they’re…from another…world. Other…worldly…*giggles*. Now it’s time for some lovey, heart-warming quotage:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“We have to make the stars align for us now—find a way for us not to get burned for being together.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“I’m working every angle I can think of to align those stars for you Kricket. I promise,” he admits. “I’ll find a way out of this for you.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“You could never be a temporary situation for me, Kricket. I know that once I have you, I’ll never be able to let you go.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Trey, all of that is meaningless. The only thing that matters is how we feel about each other. I love you and that’s never going to change,” I promise, leaning forward and placing a gentle kiss on his cheek. “I’m yours,” I whisper, shifting my lips to the other cheek and kissing it, too. “And you’re mine,” I continue looking in his eyes, before touching my lips to his.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />Now, it’s not all daisies and sunshine when it comes to the romance in this book. If you’ve read Amy Bartol’s Preomonition Series, you know that she writes some great villains. The kind of villains that you’re not even sure if you love, hate, or want to take to bed just to get them out of your system. Enter: Kyon. Ah yes, he is bad to the bone from the very start, and he’s pompous, arrogant, conniving, and manipulative…and he looks damn good doing it, too. Naturally Kyon has his sights on Kricket, and he will go to any means just to have her. Not on Trey’s watch…<br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“You’re so passionate and resolute. How could I possibly let you go?” Kyon is still smiling. Frowning, Trey says in a deadly tone, “I’ll make you see that letting her go is the only option available to you.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />This book was 100% certifiably FANTASTIC. This was such an entertaining read, fast-paced, entertaining, with enough sexual tension to get your juices flowing. I find that when reading books within the Sci-fi genre, at times the plot can get lost in the world building. This was not the case with this book. The dialect, the imagery, and the characters, were all interesting and well developed. I felt transported into another realm, all while being captivated by a story that left me unable to put this book down.<br /><br />Amy A. Bartol is one of those writers who tends to leave no stone unturned when it comes to creating books that stick with you long after you read them. My first thought upon finishing Under Different Stars was “Do I have time to reread this?” I was completely and utterly HOOKED. I cannot wait until the next book comes out, and we see what is in store for Kricket and the other lovable (and not so lovable) characters. With that, I’ll leave you with a final thought from my new favorite broody book boyfriend, Trey:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“They won’t keep us apart, Kricket,” he promises. “We won’t let them.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />If you haven’t read this, you don’t know what you’re missing. There’s a whole world in here waiting for you…<br /><br /><b>5++++++ Stars!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5758756173172640078" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7359090744893143047">This genre is not something I read a lot of which is bizarre because I love watching movies and shows with a sci fi theme but throw a book into the mix and more often than not, I won't even give it a second glance. <br/><br/>But when this showed up on my doorstep and I saw the gorgeous cover and the blurb, I knew I was making one of my rare exceptions and giving it a chance. Yes I can be petty and shallow like that.<br/><br/>But oh goodness how this story completely captured my attention and held it. I was complete</span>
  <span id="freeText7359090744893143047" style="display:none">This genre is not something I read a lot of which is bizarre because I love watching movies and shows with a sci fi theme but throw a book into the mix and more often than not, I won't even give it a second glance. <br /><br />But when this showed up on my doorstep and I saw the gorgeous cover and the blurb, I knew I was making one of my rare exceptions and giving it a chance. Yes I can be petty and shallow like that.<br /><br />But oh goodness how this story completely captured my attention and held it. I was completely under the author's spell and fascinated with the world and people she had created.<br /><br />I loved feisty headstrong Kricket from the word hello and that love just grew as her character and story evolved. <br /><br />Trey was just as fabulous, and Jax and Wayra stole the show. There is something to be said about secondary characters that you want to know and love every bit as much as the main characters.<br /><br />I seriously went into this expecting nothing and getting so very much in return. I loved it and can't wait for book two to be out. I know there are so many more adventured for Trey, Kricket, Jax, and Wayra and I can't wait to take the journey with them. <br /></span>

<div id="review_795277471" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/795277471" />
    <a title="Alex Black" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26766150-alex-black"><img alt="Alex Black" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390016257p2/26766150.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/795277471?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex Black" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex Black" href="/user/show/26766150-alex-black">Alex Black</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26766150-alex-black?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26766150-alex-black?shelf=recommend">recommend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26766150-alex-black?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer795277471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8655898724737339929">I was very hesitant to read this book for two reasons – <br/>1.	I was sort of mad at Amy for writing this one before Iniquity. I am a big Premonition fan – it is one of my absolute favorite series, I just could not understand why write THIS BOOK, when Iniquity was supposed to be finished a while ago. <br/>2.	I don’t like to wait – I am impatient, and want to fully enjoy a series one book right after the other. I did not want to get sucked into another series that I would have to WAIT to see what happens n</span>
  <span id="freeText8655898724737339929" style="display:none">I was very hesitant to read this book for two reasons – <br />1.	I was sort of mad at Amy for writing this one before Iniquity. I am a big Premonition fan – it is one of my absolute favorite series, I just could not understand why write THIS BOOK, when Iniquity was supposed to be finished a while ago. <br />2.	I don’t like to wait – I am impatient, and want to fully enjoy a series one book right after the other. I did not want to get sucked into another series that I would have to WAIT to see what happens next. It is rare I start a series when only book one is out.<br />Despite my hesitations, I decided to take the risk because I love the way Amy writes. Let me tell you – the decision to read this was the best decision I have made in new book choices lately. Probably by 15% in, I was already sucked in and did not want to stop. Yes…..I did stay up til 4 AM last night to read after the family went to go to bed to only get to 60%....and despite being tired I decided that finishing the book today was much more important than a nap or doing chores around the house….so of course I had to finish it! Well, well worth the read, and yes I will be re-reading it every time before the next one comes out. I became more than sucked in…..it was more like obsessed. After reading this, I did finally decide to forgive Amy for putting a delay on Iniquity….this book was well worth the read to explore another world and characters. Heck, you gotta have something else to get excited about with Premonition coming closer to an end. Here are a few reasons why this book is one of my favorites!!<br />Kricket, the female heroine has a damaged past, but it has only made her a stronger person that never wants to give up and fights for herself. Despite her damaged past, she is clever, witty, and has a magnetic personality. I like that in this story Kricket does not have the typical love at first site. Not only has she never experienced love, but the love that makes her complete has to be earned by what she needs, but tries to deny the most – protection and also respect. Kricket is definitely my favorite type of female character, tough and courageous. Her ninja skills are not quite up to par, but she has many compensating factors…..yet, but I think it is only a matter of time. <br />I don’t want to give any spoilers for this one, but let’s say, that I definitely have a new favorite book boyfriend to add to the top of the list. The chase and the tension that builds and grows over the course of their journey to Ethar is beautiful, romantic, and irresistible. There were quite a few quotes from that I was tempted to put in this review…that just made me melt! I also love the new friendships that Kricket makes on her journey, and the respect and love that she earns from others along the way. Amy has an ease to her writing and a way with words where she does an excellent job in making Ethar appear unique but normal. You are easily transported behind the eyes of Kricket to Ethar and feel instantly at home in the new universe despite the learning curve of new lingo and Etharian terms. This book includes quality and admirable characters, full of action and suspense, creative and well thought out story line, and a passionate romance that starts with a spark and burns you to the core by the end of the book. The downside? It left me sad that it was over, but eager and desperate for more…..glad it is a series….but hope the wait it not too long! Well done, and great job Amy Bartol!<br />Like this review or want to discuss? Visit us and see more book reviews @booksbeyondtheend.com<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8655898724737339929" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1407172341" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1407172341" />
    <a title="Kenzie The Dragon Queen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42276702-kenzie-the-dragon-queen"><img alt="Kenzie The Dragon Queen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575851043p2/42276702.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1407172341?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kenzie The Dragon Queen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kenzie The Dragon Queen" href="/user/show/42276702-kenzie-the-dragon-queen">Kenzie The Dragon Queen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781477821121" href="/book/show/23109056-under-different-stars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42276702-kenzie-the-dragon-queen?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42276702-kenzie-the-dragon-queen?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42276702-kenzie-the-dragon-queen?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42276702-kenzie-the-dragon-queen?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42276702-kenzie-the-dragon-queen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42276702-kenzie-the-dragon-queen?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42276702-kenzie-the-dragon-queen?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42276702-kenzie-the-dragon-queen?shelf=books-i-have-reviewed">books-i-have-reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1407172341" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5750155062562300649"><u>Personal Note</u> <br/> <br/>This is my first ever <i>officiall</i> re-read. I only decided to re-read this book because I had originally bought it and read it nearly four years ago, and shortly after bought the sequels and then forgotten about continuing the series. In the wake of covid and self quarantine, it’s become difficult for me to start new series, because I only own the first instalment, and if I like it, then I have to wait for shipment and delivery, because I’m a book hoarder that prefers to own physical</span>
  <span id="freeText5750155062562300649" style="display:none"><u>Personal Note</u> <br /> <br />This is my first ever <i>officiall</i> re-read. I only decided to re-read this book because I had originally bought it and read it nearly four years ago, and shortly after bought the sequels and then forgotten about continuing the series. In the wake of covid and self quarantine, it’s become difficult for me to start new series, because I only own the first instalment, and if I like it, then I have to wait for shipment and delivery, because I’m a book hoarder that prefers to own physical copies of books that I like instead of just doing the sane thing and reading an e-book. Hence, this odd re-read. I now feel like I’ve backed myself into a corner by doing this re-read and therefore I absolutely have to read and finish this trilogy now so I don’t ever have to do it again.<br /> <br /> <br /> <br /><u>Review</u><br /> <br /><i>Under Different Stars</i> is an entertaining and engaging young adult science fiction space opera romance. It’s not very original or especially ambitious, and relies on a lot of retired tropes.<br /><br />I liked the protagonist, Kricket, well enough. She was sassy, witty, and sarcastic, but she’s a survivor too. Her character still fell prey to a lot of early 2010’s tropes like “oh no too many men want me” or “destiny depends on whether or not my hymen is intact” and “I’m super beautiful but I don’t know it” which were unappealing characteristics. The side characters of Jax and Wayra were cool, but felt a lot like slightly different versions of the the exact same person. The love interest, Trey, was fine if I’m being nice, and unbearable if I’m in a really bad mood. He just didn’t stand out in anyway, and could’ve been a character a robot created from reading about everyone’s favourite book boyfriends and smooshing all of their “best” traits together before stripping him down to the essentials. The villain, Kyon, was arguably the most interesting of the whole cast. He was devious and undoubtedly wicked, but usually correct. His motivations and obsession with the protagonist made him intriguing.<br /><br />The romance really fell flat for me, and I disliked it. I find it bland, passionless, lacking chemistry, rushed, and a little cheap feeling. It seemed like the author pushed the two characters together more because she wanted them to be, and less because it actually made sense or worked within the context of the finished product. It turns out that I’m in the minority on this one. Most people seem to love these two together. However, if you’re like me, and cannot stand insta-love romance for the life of you, then you’ll understand why I thought this particular romance wasn’t very good. They fall in love within a few days, then spend weeks barely interacting, and then they’re all in and completely in love? Yeah, <b>no</b>, that’s a hard pass.<br /><br />I really appreciated the effort put into the world building, but it was hit and miss. I liked how the author adjusted the planet to feel like earth enough for it to be familiar, but made it different enough to remind you that it was not. Things I liked were how the gravity and size of the planet made everything grow slightly larger, even the humans, hence why Kricket at 5’10 was considered quite small. I also really liked the cool and sleek advanced tech, mixed with some medieval and Greek period inspirations. I also enjoyed the cultures and history and how you learn so much about it all without any info dumps. However, the entire planet being misogynistic was completely unnecessary. The slang was incredibly cringeworthy. I understand that obviously they’d have different slang then humans, because they’re on a completely different planet, so it only makes sense. It was just so so so cringy! It rolled off the tongue all wrong and gave me second hand embarrassment. Some of their titles and words were swapped out for different made up words, which once again makes sense, but sometimes it was a bit hard to follow, and combined with the slang, made a lot of the dialogue stilted, odd, and unnatural. Especially when it was coming from Trey for some reason.<br /><br />Overall, the book is a good one to pick up if you’re just looking for something easy and fun to read. If you appreciate it on a surface level, it’s quite enjoyable. But as soon as you start posing morale dilemmas or questioning the logic, the story starts to fall apart. It’s a chill and entertaining read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5750155062562300649" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1195362771" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1195362771" />
    <a title="Alicia Batista (Addicted Readers)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers"><img alt="Alicia Batista (Addicted Readers)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384217885p2/14564026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1195362771?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alicia Batista (Addicted Readers)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alicia Batista (Addicted Readers)" href="/user/show/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers">Alicia Batista (Addicted Readers)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=a-must-read">a-must-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=amazing">amazing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=soliders">soliders</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=so-many-feelings">so-many-feelings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=you-ll-be-sorry-if-you-miss-this-bo">you-ll-be-sorry-if-you-miss-this-bo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=read-it">read-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=strong-female">strong-female</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1195362771" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6875962062482603585"><br/><i> <b>4 STARS</b> </i><br/><br/>Ooh boy, where do I even begin? UNDER DIFFERENT STARS was a thrilling ride that I absolutely loved! I REALLY enjoyed UNDER DIFFERENT STARS, a lot! I was hooked from the very beginning and loved the pacing of this book. I never found myself bored or wanting to put it down for something else. I always wanted to keep reading when I knew it was time to do something else. I enjoyed the characters and their sharp personalities, and the obstacles they faced. The villains were chilling enough t</span>
  <span id="freeText6875962062482603585" style="display:none"><br /><i> <b>4 STARS</b> </i><br /><br />Ooh boy, where do I even begin? UNDER DIFFERENT STARS was a thrilling ride that I absolutely loved! I REALLY enjoyed UNDER DIFFERENT STARS, a lot! I was hooked from the very beginning and loved the pacing of this book. I never found myself bored or wanting to put it down for something else. I always wanted to keep reading when I knew it was time to do something else. I enjoyed the characters and their sharp personalities, and the obstacles they faced. The villains were chilling enough to make me want to hate them, yet intriguing enough that I wanted to see what would happen if they got the upper hand. The world-building was fascinating! I thought the idea of a different planet on the verge of war all fighting to all claim the same girl with extraordinary gifts, beyond thrilling and totally engaging! The romance was right up my alley too. I'm a sucker for a good love/hate romance, with a thrilling adventure to push them together, to be nothing short of romantic. Yeah, I know, I'm weird like that...lol! But I know some people found this book too be lacking, but not me, not one bit!<br /><br />I loved Kricket to pieces. Even though she was a little too perfect, her fierce personality and strong demeanor won me over her perfectness. She looked like a barbie doll but with violet eyes. All the guys loved her and swooned over her, and wanted to become her consort (husband). But like I said, her attitude is quick-witted and fierce, and was enough to make me love her regardless of the flaws, or should I say flaw-less traits. She doesn't notice her flawless beauty, or thinks she's better then anyone, or anything like that. Plus I don't usually read books with flawless charters, so it was a nice change to my normal flawed characters.<br /><br />Her love interest Trey was definitely hot, and I found myself swooning over him from time to time. There was a lot of guys rallying for Kricket's heart, but Trey couldn't official be one of those guys, because he was ranked at lower royalty. So he pretty much wasn't on Kricket's level. But that didn't matter to either of them, they loved each other and towards the end were ready to fight for each other. Trey was very protective of Kricket, a protectiveness that went above and beyond his duties as just being her guard. I could see he generally loved her, even if in the beginning he didn't want to admit it to himself or to her.<br /><br /><i> <b>THE PLOT</b> </i><br /><br />Kricket has lived her life on the run from police, social workers, foster families, and everyone else determined to tame her. She's had her fair share of pain and abandonment since her parents died, and was forced to endure numerous horrific foster families. But Kricket has finally had enough and is on the run waiting out the last month until she becomes of age and can finally take care of herself, without having to look over her shoulder. But unfortunately, for Kricket, that never happens, because just when she thinks her life can't get anymore complicated then it is, she's kidnapped and taken under different stars...<br /><br />Kricket's always known she was different. Her eyes are violet, her hair grows back after it's cut, and she can tell when someones not being truthful. She knows it, but still she tries to blend in and only wants to turn eighteen so she can be responsible for her own self. But a month before her eighteenth birthday, three guys resembling herself with violet eyes track her down claiming they're taking her "home" to pay for her "crimes". A home she knows nothing about, a place even more controlling then the home she has now. A home that's a whole new world, under different stars...<br /><br />After being kidnapped from earth and forced to the planet Ethar, Kricket is dragged through harsh lands to make it to the capital of Skye City, where she is to be tried for her "Crimes", crimes she knows nothing about. But once she arrives, she's swept into conspires after conspires, as two house (territories) battle for possession of her, a battle she has no say in, a battle that she cannot win, because either way the outcome is the same: She will be controlled, she will be used, and she will be helpless, one way or another, unless she finds another way to beat them all at their own game...<br /><br />But through it all, she only finds solace in the hands of Trey, her kidnapper. Where he has been the only one to break through the heart of stone she has formed, and strait to the inner core of her being, and has become the one thing she desires above all else. But first she will have to fight to gain control over herself, and ward off the many men trying to claim her, and tame her.<br /><br />I can't really think of anything that I didn't enjoy, because the entire time I was glued to the pages and couldn't get enough. Amy A. Bartol has gone on my list of new favorite authors of 2015! I'm definitely eager to see what else she brings us, and curious about her first series!<br /><br />Overall, UNDER DIFFERENT STARS was a fantastic book that I absolutely adored. With no obvious reservations about it, and a plot that is addicting and thrilling, and a romance that captured my heart and has me eager for more! I can't wait to continuing this series and see how it all ends! If this review has you intrigued, then I think it's definitely worth a shot, because I was not disappointed one bit!<br /><br /><i> <b>BRING ON BOOK TWO!!!</b> </i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6875962062482603585" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1220360067?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" href="/user/show/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue">Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=why-am-i-just-now-reading-this">why-am-i-just-now-reading-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=aliens-sci-fi">aliens-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=girl-power">girl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1220360067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5085817650023295426">This is one of those cases where bloggers and reviews really do help sell books because if I hadn't seen some of my blogger friends gushing about this novel, I might never have picked it up otherwise. And I would have been missing out on a fabulous sci-fi story rife with political intrigue, romance, and some serious ass-kicking.<br/><br/>I listened to the audio, performed by Kate Rudd, and I found it impossible to stop listening once I really started it. I downloaded the audio before I left on vacation an</span>
  <span id="freeText5085817650023295426" style="display:none">This is one of those cases where bloggers and reviews really do help sell books because if I hadn't seen some of my blogger friends gushing about this novel, I might never have picked it up otherwise. And I would have been missing out on a fabulous sci-fi story rife with political intrigue, romance, and some serious ass-kicking.<br /><br />I listened to the audio, performed by Kate Rudd, and I found it impossible to stop listening once I really started it. I downloaded the audio before I left on vacation and only got a taste of it before I put it aside, but it was already pretty amazing at that point, and the whole time I was away from it, I wanted to get back to it. So, on Sunday, while I was doing all of the laundry from vacation, I put the audiobook on and never looked back. It made an otherwise hellish chore actually quite enjoyable.<br /><br />I loved Trey's stoicism, Kricket's unflappableness (if that's not a word, I'm making it one), and all of the other characters who seemed larger than life in this novel. This story was as unpredictable as it was intense, and I loved every second of it. I can't wait to read more of Kricket's adventures on Ethar when the sequel released later this month!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5085817650023295426" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2135960549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18318591858372846436"><b>UGH!</b><br/>I loved everything about this book. <br/><br/>I've seen this book pop on my recommendation list for my Kindle for like ever.. and I'm kind of shocked that I FINALLY took a chance on it. I'm freaking hooked guys and I was not prepared to feel these god damns feelings at all.<br/><br/>I loved Kricket. <br/>I loved Trey. <br/>I fucking shipped the fucking shit out of those two. Throw in Kyon and I'm rooting even more for those two - screw Kyon. <br/><br/>I wish I could be friends with someone like Kricket, well .. no. I'd like to be </span>
  <span id="freeText18318591858372846436" style="display:none"><b>UGH!</b><br />I loved everything about this book. <br /><br />I've seen this book pop on my recommendation list for my Kindle for like ever.. and I'm kind of shocked that I FINALLY took a chance on it. I'm freaking hooked guys and I was not prepared to feel these god damns feelings at all.<br /><br />I loved Kricket. <br />I loved Trey. <br />I fucking shipped the fucking shit out of those two. Throw in Kyon and I'm rooting even more for those two - screw Kyon. <br /><br />I wish I could be friends with someone like Kricket, well .. no. I'd like to be best friends with the actual Kricket. I'm be in the background forever cheering and shipping her and Trey together. Whooping when necessary and throwing rice or something whenever they had a moment of romance. <br /><br />I'm so glad that I have the second and third book on my Kindle already because I can't wait to dive into them!</span>

<div id="review_828683088" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/828683088" />
    <a title="Sylvia " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4557869-sylvia"><img alt="Sylvia " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1432475002p2/4557869.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/828683088?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sylvia " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sylvia " href="/user/show/4557869-sylvia">Sylvia </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4557869-sylvia?shelf=indie-authors">indie-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4557869-sylvia?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4557869-sylvia?shelf=bad-boys-for-the-red-room">bad-boys-for-the-red-room</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4557869-sylvia?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4557869-sylvia?shelf=another-world">another-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4557869-sylvia?shelf=romantic-suspense">romantic-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4557869-sylvia?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4557869-sylvia?shelf=dystopian-scifi-post-apocalyptic">dystopian-scifi-post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4557869-sylvia?shelf=aliens">aliens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4557869-sylvia?shelf=villains-we-hate-to-love">villains-we-hate-to-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer828683088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15033934041860349927">Started off a little slow for me at the beginning but as soon as the story progressed it took off with a <b>whoosh</b> and I was catapulted right into it. <br/><br/><i>Under Different Stars</i> is a story about Kricket Hollowell. She might seem like an average young woman but there is nothing average about her. You see, Kricket has lived it a little rough, going in and out of the foster care system, from one family to the next, never really knowing her parents. She basically is waiting until the moment she turns eighte</span>
  <span id="freeText15033934041860349927" style="display:none">Started off a little slow for me at the beginning but as soon as the story progressed it took off with a <b>whoosh</b> and I was catapulted right into it. <br /><br /><i>Under Different Stars</i> is a story about Kricket Hollowell. She might seem like an average young woman but there is nothing average about her. You see, Kricket has lived it a little rough, going in and out of the foster care system, from one family to the next, never really knowing her parents. She basically is waiting until the moment she turns eighteen, so she no longer is a ward of the state. But, the universe literally has other things in mind for her. Stalked by a couple of groups of men, one led by Trey Allairas - <i>Yes please if I may dabble with this tall drip of honey</i> - and the other by Kyon Ensin - <i>A big knob knocker who I think is going to surprise me a little in book 2, but still a knob knocker</i>, Kricket is instantly propelled into a world she knew nothing of. I had a hard time though, believing that she never really questioned the fact that she is alien and not of this earth. I mean, come on. She really handled herself like a pro, which I admired, but she just blatantly accepted what they were telling her as the truth, and because of her special gifts, she didn't doubt them for a minute. This is why I dropped a star in my ratings. A little too accepting and less questioning about her heritage. <br />Anyways, the story just kicks off once she is taken from Earth to Ethar and from that point on, I could not put it down. I really loved Kricket's ability to talk her way out of anything with so much cheek and gusto. She's one independent gal who is brave and unafraid to push the boundaries. Just the way I like characters to be i.e. unapologetic and unwavering. <br /><br />On to the next book for me, even though the ending was a nice little cliffhanger, I'm really wanting to know what's next for Kricket, Trey and Kyon, because if it's anything like what I've read so far, than I'm in for a wild and adventurous ride. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15033934041860349927" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ufeC1eBSvCL90Nj5B9hodaKOMvVRJjOr8HbiwVSSYAnKXqx9Yzym55bKfx0qyVw1eMAodPwaRajZYz6IWzKukw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nL9ld3S7eCjJYsZSzv+0jCMUILdg21zBL5RBGExMS6vvFkvf99Vi7aJ4Ybbj7oDM+Vo6Ns3nKsIGgZ1RQ+yFMQ==')})
  }
//]]>

  <span id="freeText9883939462098535340" style="display:none">Author of the Secondborn Series:<br />Secondborn (Book 1)<br />Traitor Born (Book 2)<br />Rebel Born (Book 3) <br /><br />Author of the Premonition Series:<br />Inescapable (Book 1) <br />Intuition (Book 2)<br />Indebted (Book 3)<br />Incendiary (Book 4) <br />Iniquity (Book 5) <br /><br />Author of the Kricket Series:<br />Under Different Stars (Book 1) <br />Sea of Stars (Book 2)<br />Darken the Stars (Book 3)<br /><br />The Divided - A Science Fiction Romance short story, which is included in the Take Me To Your Reader: An Otherworld Anthology. <br /><br />Amy A. Bartol is the USA Today and Wall Street Journal bestselling author of The Secondborn Series, The Premonition Series, The Kricket Series, and a short story entitled “The Divided.” She has won numerous awards for her writing and been nominated for several more. She's a graduate of Hillsdale College, which inspired the setting of her Premonition Series. Amy lives in Michigan with her husband and two sons, but she travels often, sparking her imagination to create more worlds like the ones with hidden angels, doorways to alien landscapes, and fantastical futuristic societies and technologies.
